$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Working/MonitorRGB=Monitor RGB:  Sets the RGB working space to your current monitor space.  This setting causes Photoshop to behave as if color management were turned off.  Use this setting if other applications in your workflow do not support color management.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Preset=^1:  ^2
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Working=Working Spaces:  The working space specifies the working color profile for each color model.  (A color profile defines how a color^}s numeric values map to its visual appearance.)  The working space is used for documents that are not color-managed, and for newly created documents that are color-managed.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/WorkingRGB=Working RGB:  Specifies the working RGB profile.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/WorkingCMYK=Working CMYK:  Specifies the working CMYK profile.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/WorkingGray=Working Gray:  Specifies the working gray profile.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/WorkingSpot=Working Spot:  Specifies the dot gain to use when displaying spot color channels and duotones.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Policies=Color Management Policies:  Policies specify how you want colors in a particular color model managed.  Policies handle the reading and embedding of color profiles, mismatches between embedded color profiles and the working space, and the moving of colors from one document to another.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Policy/Off=Off:  Turns off color management for newly created documents and for newly opened documents that have embedded color profiles different from the current working space.  If a newly opened document^}s embedded color profile matches the current working space, that profile is preserved.  When importing colors into a document, the numeric values of the colors take precedence over the color appearance.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Policy/Preserve=Preserve Embedded Profiles:  Preserves the embedded color profile in a newly opened document even if the color profile does not match the current working space.  When importing colors into an RGB or grayscale document, color appearance takes precedence over the numeric values of the colors.  When importing colors into a CMYK document, numeric values take precedence over the appearance.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Policy/Convert=Convert to Working Space:  Converts a newly opened document to the current working space if that document^}s embedded color profile does not match the working space.  When importing colors into a document, color appearance takes precedence over the numeric values of the colors.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/ProfileMismatches=Profile Mismatches:  Specifies when you want to be notified about profile mismatches.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/AskOpening=Profile Mismatches - Ask When Opening:  When enabled, you will be notified whenever the embedded color profile in a newly opened document does not match the current working space, and given the option to override the policy^}s default mismatch behavior.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/AskPasting=Profile Mismatches - Ask When Pasting:  When enabled, you will be notified whenever color profile mismatches occur as colors are imported into a document (via pasting, drag-and-drop, etc.), and given the option to override the policy^}s default mismatch behavior.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/AskMissing=Missing Profiles - Ask When Opening:  When enabled, and the corresponding policy is not off, you will be notified whenever you open an existing document without an embedded profile, and given the option to assign a color profile.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Conversion=Conversion Options:  Specifies details on how you want color space conversions performed.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine/ACE=Uses the Adobe color management system and color engine.  Recommended for most users.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine/ColorSync=Uses the Apple ColorSync color management system and its default color matching method.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine/ColorSync/CMM=Uses the Apple ColorSync color management system and this color matching method.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine/ICM=Uses the Microsoft ICM color management system and its default color matching method.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine/ICM/CMM=Uses the Microsoft ICM color management system and this color matching method.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine/Template=^1:  ^2
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Engine=Engine:  The Engine setting specifies the Color Management System (CMS) or Color Matching Method (CMM) used to convert colors between color spaces.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Intent=Intent:  The rendering intent specifies the method used to convert colors between color spaces.  Note that the result of choosing a rendering intent depends on the profiles used to specify the color spaces.  (Some profiles produce identical results with different rendering intents.)
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Intent/Perceptual=Perceptual:  Requests a visually pleasing rendering, preserving the visual relationships between source colors.  Often used to render wide gamut source images, where preserving the relationship of colors inside and outside the destination gamut is more important than exactly matching the colors inside the destination gamut.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Intent/RelColor=Relative Colorimetric:  Attempts to match the media-relative Lab coordinates of the destination colors to the media-relative Lab coordinates of the source colors.  The source white point is mapped to the destination white point.  Recommended for most color conversions, especially when most source colors are already inside the destination gamut.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Intent/Saturation=Saturation:  Requests a highly saturated rendering, at the possible expense of color accuracy.  Mostly used for business graphics (pie charts, etc.), where color accuracy is less important than having a highly saturated result.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Intent/AbsColor=Absolute Colorimetric:  Attempts to match the absolute Lab coordinates of the destination colors to the absolute Lab coordinates of the source colors.  Does not adjust for different media white points.  Mostly used for ^[logo^] colors, and for hard proofing.  Not recommended for most color conversions.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/MapBlack=Use Black Point Compensation:  Controls whether to adjust for differences in black points when converting colors between color spaces.  When enabled, the full dynamic range of the source space is mapped into the full dynamic range of the destination space.  When disabled, the dynamic range of the source space is simulated in the destination space (which can result in blocked or gray shadows).
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Dither=Use Dither:  Controls whether to dither colors when converting 8-bit-per-channel images between color spaces.  Dithering greatly reduces banding artifacts, but may increase file size.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/CompensateProfile=Apply video contrast rendering when converting between scene- & output-referred color profiles. Enable this option to match After Effects CS4 and later default color management. 
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/AdvancedControls=Advanced Controls:  Monitor compression and color blending controls.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/SuiteColorSyncInBridge=To synchronize color settings among your Creative Cloud applications, select Color Settings in Bridge.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Compression=Desaturate Monitor Colors By:  Controls whether to desaturate colors when they are displayed on the monitor.  When enabled this setting can aid in visualizing the full range of color spaces with gamuts larger than that of the monitor.  However, the monitor display will no longer match the printed output.  This setting is recommended for expert users only.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/BlendGamma=Blend RGB Colors Using Gamma:  Controls the blending behavior of RGB colors.  When enabled, RGB colors are blended using the specified gamma.  A gamma of 1.00 is considered to be ^[colorimetricly correct^] and should result in the fewest edge artifacts.  When disabled, RGB colors are blended directly in the document^}s color space; this behavior matches the algorithm used by most other applications.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/TextBlendGamma=Blend Text Colors Using Gamma:  Controls the blending behavior of text layers.  When enabled, text colors are blended using the specified gamma.
$$$/ColorSettings/Message/Message=Description:  Move the cursor over the item you want described.  If you want to change the description for the current color settings, press the ^[Save...^] button.
$$$/ColorSettings/Synchronized=Synchronized: Your Creative Cloud applications are synchronized using the same color settings for consistent color management.
$$$/ColorSettings/NotSynchronized=Unsynchronized: Your Creative Cloud applications are not synchronized for consistent color.

$$$/Prefs/3D/ToolTip/GPUMemoryUsage=Available VRAM for 3D: Amount of video memory (VRAM) that Photoshop 3D Forge (3D engine) is allowed to use.^nThis does not affect OS and general Photoshop VRAM allocation - it strictly sets the maximum VRAM 3D is allowed to use. $$$/Prefs/3D/ToolTip/Interaction=Interactive Rendering: Specifies Photoshop preferences for rendering options during interaction (mouse-down) of 3D objects.^nAllow Direct To Screen: Direct to Screen allows for faster 3D interaction as it draws pixels directly to screen leveraging your GPU graphics card. If your graphics card is not robust enough or you have your Drawing Mode (Preferences > Performance > Graphics Processor Setting: Advanced) set to Basic, you may experience large color shifts during interaction.Turning this option off may resolve this issue. Note that interaction will be slower with this turned off.^nAuto Hide Layers: Automatically hides all layers except for the current 3D layer for fastest interaction.
$$$/Prefs/3D/ToolTip/3DShadowQuality=Shadow Quality: Specifies Photoshop preferences for rendering shadows during OpenGL preview of the rendering. ^nHigher Quality means a better shadow boundary, at the expense of higher VRAM consumption.^nLower Quality could mean potential 'jagged' shadow boundaries at grazing light angles.  However, lower quality utilizes less GPU resources, with lower VRAM consumption and possibly higher interactive frame rates.^nNOTE: These settings do not affect the shadows during ray trace rendering (activated by the 3D -> Render menu item), only the shadows during interactive preview.

$$$/Prefs/3D/ToolTip/FileLoading=3D File Loading: Specifies behaviors when 3D files are loaded.^nActive Light Source Limit: Sets the initial limit for active lights. If the number of light sources in the incoming 3D file exceeds the limit, some light sources will be initially turned off. The user can still turn them on in the 3D Panel using the eye icon next to the light source object in a Scene view.^nDefault Diffuse Texture Limit: Sets the maximum number of diffuse textures that Photoshop will auto-generate on materials when diffuse textures are absent. If your 3D file has a material count that exceeds this number, Photoshop will not auto-generate textures. Diffuse textures are necessary for painting on 3D.  However, Photoshop will prompt you to create a texture if you are painting on a material without one.

$$$/PrintPreview/Message/Perceptual=Aims to preserve the visual relationship between colors so the colors are perceived as natural to the human eye, even though the color values themselves may change. This intent is suitable for photographic images with out-of-gamut colors.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/Saturation=Tries to produce vivid colors in an image at the expense of color accuracy. This rendering intent is suitable for business graphics like graphs or charts, where bright saturated colors are more important than the exact relationship between colors (such as in a photographic image).
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/RelativeColorimetric=Compares the white of the source color space to that of the destination color space and shifts all colors accordingly. Out-of-gamut colors are shifted to the closest reproducible color in the destination color space. Relative colorimetric preserves more of the original colors in an image than Perceptual.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/AbsoluteColorimetric=Colors that fall inside the destination gamut are unchanged. Out-of-gamut colors are shifted to the closest reproducible color. No scaling of colors to destination white point is performed. This intent maintains color accuracy at the expense of preserving relationships between colors, and is suitable for proofing to simulate the output of a particular device.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/PrinterPerc=Instruct the printer to try to preserve the visual relationship between colors so the colors are perceived as natural to the human eye. This intent is suitable for photographic images with out-of-gamut colors. Not all printers honor this setting.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/PrinterSat=Instruct the printer to attempt to produce vivid colors suitable for business graphics like graphs or charts. Not all printers honor this setting.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/PrinterRC=Instruct the printer to shift all colors in order to move out-of-gamut colors to the closest reproducible color in the destination color space. Not all printers honor this setting.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/PrinterAC=Instruct the printer to shift out-of-gamut colors to the closest reproducible color, and leave in-gamut colors unchanged. Not all printers honor this setting.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/RISeps=No rendering intent can be specified when printing separations.
$$$/PrintPreview/Message/BlackPointCompensation=Adjusts for differences in black points when converting colors.
